13.3 Configuration Type by Recipe

Type I: Linear Transition

Maximum flexibility, minimal self-maintenance, easy reversal

Protection: Integration (8.1.4), Extension (8.6.1) Self-Cleansing (8.1.1b), Recovery (8.1.2b), Sanctuary Purging (8.2.3b) Portability (8.2.4b), Gatekeeping (8.3.1b), Reception (8.3.2b) Filter and Redirect (8.3.3b), Disrupting Attacks (8.4.1b), Concealment (8.4.5b) Finance: Daily Abundance Flow (9.4.2) Clearing Financial Fear (9.1.1b), Discernment (9.3.3b), Opening to Receive (9.4.1b) Self-Development: Radical Self-Honesty (10.1.1b), Shadow Integration (10.1.2b) Openness to Magick (10.2.1b), Openness to Divine Knowledge (10.2.2b) Developing Intuition (10.2.3b), Recognizing Opportunity (10.3.2b) Love: Releasing Attachment Patterns (11.2.1b), Receptivity to Love (11.3.1b) Attracting Right Relationship (11.3.2b), Boundaries in Love (11.3.3b)

Type II: Origin Reinforcement

Momentum from starting point, moderate persistence

Protection: (None) Finance: Relationship with Money Healing (9.2.3) Opening to Receive (9.4.1c) Self-Development: (None in primary workings) Love: Healing Past Relationship Wounds (11.1.4)

Type III: Destination Locking

Self-maintaining, requires active reversal — most common type

Protection (15 workings): Self-Cleansing (8.1.1), Recovery (8.1.2), Energy Reclamation (8.1.3) Sanctuary Establishment (8.2.1), Sanctuary Maintenance (8.2.2) Sanctuary Purging (8.2.3), Portability (8.2.4) Gatekeeping (8.3.1), Reception (8.3.2), Filter and Redirect (8.3.3) Disrupting Attacks (8.4.1), Manifestation Buffering (8.4.2) Resonance Attenuation (8.4.3), Return to Sender (8.4.4), Concealment (8.4.5) Bond Breaking (8.5.1a) Finance (12 workings): Clearing Financial Fear (9.1.1), Releasing Guilt (9.1.2), Breaking Scarcity (9.1.3) Abundance Mindset (9.2.1), Financial Self-Worth (9.2.2) Financial Discipline (9.3.1), Recognizing Financial Opportunity (9.3.2), Discernment (9.3.3) Opening to Receive (9.4.1a), Generosity Flow (9.4.3), Financial Boundaries (9.5.2) Financial Sovereignty (9.5.3) Self-Development (12 workings): Radical Self-Honesty (10.1.1a), Shadow Integration (10.1.2a), Ego Right-Sizing (10.1.3) Openness to Magick (10.2.1a), Openness to Divine Knowledge (10.2.2a) Developing Intuition (10.2.3a), Discernment (10.3.1) Recognizing Opportunity (10.3.2a), Breaking Self-Limiting Patterns (10.3.3) Cultivating Discipline (10.4.1), Commitment to Growth (10.4.2) Integration After Breakthrough (10.4.3) Love (14 workings): Cultivating Self-Love (11.1.1), Softening the Heart (11.1.2) Releasing Ego in Relationship (11.1.3) Releasing Attachment Patterns (11.2.1a), Forgiveness (11.2.2) Releasing Past Relationships (11.2.3) Receptivity to Love (11.3.1a), Attracting Right Relationship (11.3.2a) Boundaries in Love (11.3.3a) Honest Communication (11.4.1), Deep Listening (11.4.2), Deepening Intimacy (11.5.1) Cultivating Mutual Respect (11.4.3a), Sustaining Passion (11.5.2b), Growing Together (11.5.3b)

Type IV: Absolute Identity

Maximum permanence, sealed state — use sparingly

Protection: Sanctuary Establishment (8.2.1b), Bond Breaking (8.5.1b) Finance: Wealth Accumulation (9.5.1a) Self-Development: (None — self-development benefits from adaptability) Love: Sustaining Passion (11.5.2a) Growing Together (11.5.3a)

13.5 Spatial Reference

Great Table Layout

Upper Left: Red (Sovereignty/Manifestation) Upper Right: White (Purification/Clarity) Lower Left: Black (Dissolution/Shadow) Lower Right: Green (Growth/Generation)

Subangle Structure

Row 1: Kerubic Section (excluding column 3) Row 2: Calvary Cross Arms Column 3: Calvary Cross Spine Rows 3-6: Servient Section (excluding column 3)

Servient Elemental Attributions

Macro (Row): Row 3: Air Row 4: Water Row 5: Earth Row 6: Fire Micro (Column): Column 1: Air Column 2: Water Column 4: Earth Column 5: Fire

Tablet of Union Prefixes

By Watchtower (Macro/Vertical): Red: a, e, x, r, p White: o, h, C, m, a Black: n, n, a, T, a Green: t, b, i, o, m By Subangle (Micro/Horizontal): Red: e, h, n, b White: x, C, a, i Black: r, m, T, o Green: p, a, a, m

13.6 Working Sequence Quick Reference

See Part XII for complete sequences. Summary of key sequences:

Protection Sequences

Establishing New Sanctuary: 8.1.1 → 8.2.1 → 8.3.1 → 8.3.2 After an Attack: 8.4.1 → 8.1.2 → 8.1.3 → 8.2.2 Ending Toxic Relationship: 8.5.1 → 8.1.4 → 8.1.1 → 8.1.3 Complete Energetic Reset: 8.5.1 → 8.1.4 → 8.1.3 → 8.1.1 → 8.2.3 → 8.2.1

Finance Sequences

Healing Money Relationship: 9.1.1 → 9.1.2 → 9.2.3 → 9.2.1 Scarcity to Prosperity: 9.1.3 → 9.2.2 → 9.3.1 → 9.4.1 → 9.5.1 Financial Sovereignty: 9.1.1 → 9.3.2 → 9.5.2 → 9.5.3

Self-Development Sequences

Love Sequences

13.7 Reversal Approach Reference

By Configuration Type

Type I (Linear Transition): Often self-reverses through natural decay DECAY approach usually sufficient Active reversal optional Type II (Origin Reinforcement): TRANSFORM approach recommended Redirect momentum rather than fight it Single-phase reversal usually sufficient Type III (Destination Locking): Requires active DISMANTLE approach May need multi-phase reversal for complex workings Cannot rely on natural decay Type IV (Absolute Identity): DISMANTLE is only option Multi-phase reversal often necessary Consider carefully before creating

Reversal Approaches

DISMANTLE: Active deconstruction via new working Use for: Type III, Type IV, urgent reversals Mechanism: Direct opposition to locked state TRANSFORM: Redirect via superseding working Use for: Type II, when energy can be redirected Mechanism: New direction subsumes old momentum DECAY: Allow natural dissolution Use for: Type I, Type V reversals Mechanism: Withdraw maintenance, let working fade

13.8 Glossary

ALCHEMICAL COLORS: The four transformational forces—Black (dissolution), White (purification), Green (growth), Red (manifestation). These determine WHAT transforms.

ARCHANGEL OF ARCHANGELS: The central Tablet of Union entity (AONT/ONTA/NTAO/TAON) representing Divine Authority. Derived from the Macro elemental attribution.

CALVARY CROSS: The cross-shaped structure within each Subangle, consisting of the Commanding Angel (Row 2, horizontal) and Summoning Angel (Column 3, vertical). Provided by the Host dyad.

CACODAEMON: One of four consequence-carrying entities in each working—Kerubic Regent, Kerubic Rooted, Servient Regent, Servient Rooted. They represent consequences and reactions to the working's action.

CHARGE: The spoken declaration that focuses intent and completes the working. Delivered after reciting the prayer.

CLASS: A category describing the relationship between a dyad's Outer and Inner forces. Class 0 (identity), Class +1 (progressive), Class -1 (regressive), Class ±2 (opposition).

COMMANDING ANGEL: The 5-letter angel derived from Row 2 of the grafted Subangle. Part of the Calvary Cross, representing Divine Compelling Will.

CONFIGURATION TYPE: The relationship pattern among Host, Initial Graft, and Terminal Graft. Types I through V, determining persistence and reversal difficulty.

DYAD: A directional pair of forces written as Outer --> Inner. The fundamental unit of operation in the system.

ELEMENTAL (E): The elemental dyad that determines HOW transformation manifests—through mental (Air), emotional (Water), structural (Earth), or active (Fire) modes.

GRAFTING: The procedure of combining columns from different Subangles around a Host's Calvary Cross to create a composite working structure.

GREAT TABLE: The complete Tabula Recensa containing four Watchtowers, each with four Subangles. The master structure from which all workings derive.

HOST (H): The alchemical dyad providing the Calvary Cross and governing meta-environment for the working.

INITIAL GRAFT (I): The alchemical dyad providing columns representing the starting state of transformation.

INNER: The emerging intention within a dyad. Synonymous with Micro. The second element in "Outer --> Inner" notation.

KERUBIC ANGEL: The 4-letter angel derived from Row 1 of the grafted Subangle (excluding Column 3). Represents connection to the ethereal realm.

MACRO: The dominant context or container force. Synonymous with Outer. Watchtower level for alchemical; Row level for elemental.

MICRO: The emerging intention. Synonymous with Inner. Subangle level for alchemical; Column level for elemental.

OUTER: The dominant context or container force within a dyad. Synonymous with Macro. The first element in "Outer --> Inner" notation.

PERFECT RESONANCE: When the elemental dyad exactly matches the translation of an alchemical dyad. Amplifies effects but can compound risk.

PRAYER: The structured invocation calling all angel names in proper sequence, activating the working's machinery.

PRINCE: The 5-letter angel derived from a spiral pattern around the Calvary Cross. Distributes power from the Watchtower hierarchy to the Subangle.

REVERSAL: A working designed to undo or release a previous working. Every recipe includes a reversal configuration.

RULING ANGEL: The 5-letter angel derived from a vertical column of the grafted Subangle. Bridges the Kerubic and Servient circuits.

SERVIENT ANGEL: The 4-letter angel determined by your Elemental dyad, representing connection to corporeal reality.

SUBANGLE: One of four quadrants within each Watchtower, containing 6 rows × 5 columns of letters from which names are derived.

SUMMONING ANGEL: The 6-letter angel derived from Column 3 of the grafted Subangle. Part of the Calvary Cross, representing Divine Authority.

TABLET OF UNION: The central 4×5 letter grid providing Archangelic prefixes and the three Archangels called in the prayer.

TERMINAL GRAFT (T): The alchemical dyad providing columns representing the achieved/end state of transformation.

TRANSLATION: The correspondence between alchemical and elemental domains (Red↔Air, Black↔Water, White↔Earth, Green↔Fire).

WATCHTOWER: One of four quadrants of the Great Table, each governed by one alchemical color at the Macro level.

• • •

End of Part XIII: Quick Reference

Appendices

Detailed theoretical reference materials for understanding the system mechanics.

• • •

Appendix A: Configuration Types

Understanding the five configuration types is essential for designing your own workings. Configuration type determines how your working behaves over time, how self-maintaining it is, and how difficult it will be to reverse.

A.1 What Configuration Type Means

Configuration type describes the RELATIONSHIP between three alchemical dyads: H = Host (the governing meta-environment) I = Initial Graft (the starting state) T = Terminal Graft (the ending state) The Elemental Dyad (E) does NOT participate in configuration type. It defines HOW the work happens, but configuration type is determined solely by the relationships among H, I, and T. There are exactly five possible relationship patterns: Type I: All three are different (H ≠ I ≠ T) Type II: Host matches start (H = I, both differ from T) Type III: Host matches end (H = T, both differ from I) Type IV: All three match (H = I = T) Type V: Grafts match, host differs (H differs from I = T)

A.2 Type I: Linear Transition

Structure: H ≠ I ≠ T (all different)

Mechanical Properties: • Pattern is NOT self-reinforcing • Host provides neutral or contrasting environment • Working requires some active maintenance to persist • Natural decay occurs when reinforcement ceases • Maximum flexibility in execution and reversal What This Creates: The transformation happens under external governance. The environment shapes but does not lock the change. Think of it as working in a rented space. When to Use: • Exploratory work where you want flexibility • Learning arcs where the outcome may need adjustment • Healing processes that should complete and release • Any working where you want the pattern to fade naturally Reversal: Easiest. Simply ceasing to reinforce often allows natural decay.

A.3 Type II: Origin Reinforcement

Structure: H = I, both differ from T

Mechanical Properties: • Starting state is amplified by host reinforcement • Departure from established ground has momentum • Creates "launching pad" effect • Moderate persistence (stronger than Type I) • The beginning is home; the ending is the journey What This Creates: Your current state or existing strength becomes the foundation from which transformation launches. Think of it as building an addition onto your house. When to Use: • Expansion from existing strength • Extending established patterns or authority • Building on what you already have • Scaling existing sovereignty or capability Reversal: Moderate difficulty. Returning to origin is natural since it's already law.

A.4 Type III: Destination Locking

Structure: H = T, both differ from I

Mechanical Properties: • Achieved state becomes self-maintaining • Creates recursive stabilization • High persistence (self-reinforcing) • Natural decay is insufficient for reversal • The destination is baked into reality What This Creates: The ending state does not merely happen—it becomes the new ambient reality that enforces itself. Think of the destination having gravity that holds you there. Special Subtype: Mirror Inversion When I and T are exact reversals (X→Y becoming Y→X) and H = T, you create a self-correcting feedback loop. Extremely powerful for protection and sovereignty. When to Use: • Sovereignty installation • Protection workings that should maintain themselves • Identity-level shifts that should persist • Creating new baseline states Reversal: Difficult. Must break host-graft unity through active intervention.

A.5 Type IV: Absolute Identity

Structure: H = I = T (all same)

Mechanical Properties: • Total fixation, no motion permitted • Self-reinforcing from all angles • Change is structurally prevented • Maximum persistence (requires external force to break) • Natural decay is impossible What This Creates: A sealed state where change cannot occur. Reality is locked into this pattern until external force is applied to break it. Critical Consideration: Type IV cannot adapt. What you lock stays locked. Use only when you genuinely need permanence, and always have a reversal strategy prepared. When to Use: • Absolute boundaries (protection from severe abuse) • Seals and wards on bounded spaces • Complete severance of bonds • When adaptation would be harmful Reversal: Most difficult. No internal leverage—must apply external force.

A.6 Type V: Parallel Reinforcement

Structure: H differs from I = T

Mechanical Properties: • Grafts maintain themselves against host pressure • Not self-locking (requires active maintenance) • Creates definition through opposition • Moderate persistence • Forge-tempering logic: pressure creates resilience What This Creates: A state that holds steady despite environmental opposition. Think of standing firm in wind—stable through effort, not fixation. When to Use: • Maintaining states in hostile environments • Holding vision despite opposition • Creative flow in rigid contexts • Discipline under temptation • Integrity work Reversal: Moderate. Remove opposition pressure or redirect with supportive host.

A.7 Configuration Type Selection Guide

Question 1: How long should this working persist? Temporary, should fade naturally → Type I Should persist but remain adaptable → Type II or Type V Should persist and self-maintain → Type III Must be permanent and unchangeable → Type IV Question 2: Do I need the result to maintain itself? No, I will maintain it or let it fade → Type I, II, or V Yes, it should run without attention → Type III It must be sealed against all change → Type IV Question 3: Am I building on existing strength or creating new? Extending what I already have → Type II Creating a new stable state → Type III Exploring or experimenting → Type I Holding against opposition → Type V Sealing permanently → Type IV Question 4: How easy should reversal be? Easy reversal is important → Type I Moderate reversal difficulty is fine → Type II or Type V Reversal should require effort → Type III Reversal should be very difficult → Type IV

A.8 Configuration Type Quick Reference

TYPE STRUCTURE PERSISTENCE REVERSAL USE FOR ──────── ───────────── ───────────── ───────────── ────────────────── Type I H ≠ I ≠ T Low Easy Exploration, flexibility Type II H = I ≠ T Moderate Moderate Expansion from strength Type III H = T ≠ I High Difficult Self-maintaining results Type IV H = I = T Maximum Very difficult Seals, vows, permanence Type V H ≠ I = T Moderate Moderate Maintaining against pressure

• • •

Appendix B: Class Structure and Selection

Every dyad belongs to one of four classes based on the relationship between its Outer and Inner components. Understanding class structure enables you to select dyads that match your intent and control the intensity of your workings.

B.1 The Canonical Ordering

Class structure is based on a canonical sequence: ALCHEMICAL: Black (1) → White (2) → Green (3) → Red (4) → [Black] ELEMENTAL: Air (1) → Water (2) → Earth (3) → Fire (4) → [Air] These orderings are STRUCTURAL, not prescriptive. They establish class relationships but do NOT mandate progression order. Any transition is valid.

B.2 Class 0: Identity

Inner = Outer (same force on both sides)

Alchemical Members: Black→Black (pure dissolution), White→White (pure purification) Green→Green (pure growth), Red→Red (pure sovereignty) Elemental Members: Air→Air (pure mentality), Water→Water (pure emotionality) Earth→Earth (pure grounding), Fire→Fire (pure action) Semantic Property: Self-reinforcing stasis, fixation, no internal motion What It Creates: • Reinforcement of a single force • Maximum intensity of that one quality • Resistance to change When to Use: Seals, wards, maximum intensity, anchoring states Risk: Compounds fixation when multiple Class 0 dyads combine

B.3 Class +1: Progressive

Inner is +1 position forward in canonical sequence

Alchemical Members: Black→White (dissolution enabling purification) White→Green (purification enabling growth) Green→Red (growth enabling manifestation) Red→Black (sovereignty enabling dissolution) Elemental Members: Air→Water (thought flowing to emotion) Water→Earth (emotion grounding to structure) Earth→Fire (structure igniting to action) Fire→Air (action clarifying to thought) Semantic Property: Developmental flow, organic progression, natural next step What It Creates: Forward motion, natural development, momentum building When to Use: Developmental processes, gradual change, learning arcs, skill building Risk: Generally safe. Low risk profile. Can feel slow if breakthrough needed.

B.4 Class -1: Regressive

Inner is -1 position backward in canonical sequence

Alchemical Members: White→Black (purification through dissolution) Green→White (growth through purification) Red→Green (sovereignty through growth) Black→Red (dissolution through sovereignty) Elemental Members: Air→Fire (thought returning to action) Water→Air (emotion returning to clarity) Earth→Water (structure returning to flow) Fire→Earth (action returning to grounding) Semantic Property: Corrective motion, return, grounding, conservation What It Creates: Return to previous phase, grounding, conservation of essence When to Use: Error correction, grounding, integration, returning to fundamentals Risk: Generally safe and stabilizing. Provides grounding for complex work.

B.5 Class +/-2: Opposition

Inner skips one position (opposite side of the wheel)

Alchemical Members: Black→Green (dissolution bridging to growth) White→Red (purification bridging to sovereignty) Green→Black (growth bridging to dissolution) Red→White (sovereignty bridging to purification) Elemental Members: Air→Earth (thought bridging to grounding) Water→Fire (emotion bridging to action) Earth→Air (grounding bridging to thought) Fire→Water (action bridging to emotion) Semantic Property: Dialectical tension, skip-level bridging, productive paradox What It Creates: Skip-level motion, integration of opposites, quantum leaps When to Use: Breakthrough workings, integrating opposites, sophisticated work Risk: Higher complexity. Creates tension that can be productive or destabilizing.

B.6 Verb-to-Class Mapping

BLACK FORCE VERBS: dissolve, release, clear, break down, strip away, let go, surrender, confront shadow, face fear, expose, reveal foundation, entropy WHITE FORCE VERBS: purify, clarify, refine, simplify, distill, cleanse, crystallize, separate, filter, essence, precision GREEN FORCE VERBS: grow, expand, proliferate, open, multiply, generate, create, birth, develop, evolve, connect, network, spread, fertile, abundant RED FORCE VERBS: manifest, embody, claim, establish, realize, sovereign, authority, throne, rule, command, complete, fulfill, incarnate, actualize CLASS INTENSITY INDICATORS: Class 0: pure, absolute, total, complete, only, nothing but, maximum Class +1: grow, develop, evolve, gradual, organic, step by step Class -1: return, come back, ground, simplify, integrate, fundamental Class +/-2: breakthrough, quantum, unlimited, leap, bridge, transform

B.7 Class Quick Reference

CLASS DEFINITION MOTION TYPE USE FOR ──────── ───────────────── ──────────────── ─────────────────────── Class 0 Inner = Outer Stasis/Fixation Seals, purity, maximum intensity Class +1 Inner +1 forward Progressive Development, growth, natural evolution Class -1 Inner -1 backward Regressive Return, correction, grounding, essence Class +/-2 Inner skips one Dialectical Breakthrough, bridging extremes, paradox

• • •

Appendix C: Elemental Resonance

The elemental dyad creates a resonance relationship with your alchemical configuration that can amplify, support, or counterbalance the working. Understanding resonance enables strategic elemental selection.

C.1 The Translation Layer

A precise correspondence exists between alchemical colors and elemental forces: Red = Air Black = Water White = Earth Green = Fire This is MECHANICAL TRANSLATION between the Spirit domain (alchemical colors) and the Elemental domain (operational forces). Why This Exists: The Tablet of Union is the interface between domains. When you provide alchemical intent (colors), that intent must TRANSLATE into elemental operation (forces) to manifest. Critical Discovery: Class structure is PRESERVED under translation. Alchemical Class 0 → Elemental Class 0 Alchemical Class +1 → Elemental Class +1 (etc.) Example: Black→White is Class +1 (alchemical) Translates to Water→Earth, which is also Class +1 (elemental)

C.2 The Three Resonance Types

PERFECT RESONANCE Definition: Elemental dyad EXACTLY MATCHES the translation of an alchemical dyad Effect: Maximum alignment between intent and manifestation Amplifies the matched dyad's properties Can compound both power AND risk Use when: Maximum alignment serves the working Caution: Perfect Resonance with risky dyads compounds the risk CLASS RESONANCE Definition: Elemental dyad has SAME CLASS but different content Effect: Structural support without identical content Provides coherence with diversity Lower risk of compounding Use when: Safe default for most workings This is often the best choice for practitioners learning to design workings CLASS DIVERGENCE Definition: Elemental dyad has DIFFERENT CLASS than alchemical dyads Effect: Cross-grain pressure between domains Can mitigate risky alchemical configurations Creates forge-tempering dynamic Use when: To ground volatile work (stable elemental) To add complexity to simple work For advanced workings requiring domain tension

C.3 Strategic Elemental Selection

FOR MAXIMUM POWER / ALIGNMENT: Strategy: Perfect Resonance with primary alchemical dyad Effect: Maximum coherence and amplification Risk: Compounds any risks in that dyad FOR SAFE, SUPPORTIVE OPERATION: Strategy: Class Resonance Effect: Structural support without compounding Risk: Low — default choice, especially while learning FOR RISK MITIGATION: Strategy: Class Divergence with stable elemental Effect: Grounds volatile alchemical work Use: When alchemical configuration is intense (Class +/-2, Type IV, heavy Black) FOR BREAKING FIXATION: Strategy: Class Divergence with progressive elemental Effect: Operational flow counterbalances alchemical stasis Use: To soften fixation or add movement to sealed patterns FOR SOPHISTICATED INTEGRATION: Strategy: Class Divergence with dialectical elemental Effect: Skip-level bridging at operational level Use: When working requires integration of opposites

C.4 Resonance Quick Reference

COLOR-ELEMENT TRANSLATION: Red = Air | Black = Water | White = Earth | Green = Fire RESONANCE TYPE IDENTIFICATION: Elemental matches alchemical translation exactly → Perfect Resonance Elemental class matches alchemical class → Class Resonance Elemental class differs from alchemical class → Class Divergence STRATEGIC SELECTION GUIDE: Goal Elemental Strategy ────────────────────────── ──────────────────────────────────── Maximum alignment Perfect Resonance with key dyad Safe default Class Resonance Risk mitigation Class Divergence (stable elemental) Breaking fixation Class +1 elemental with Class 0 alchemical Grounding complexity Class 0 elemental with Class +/-2 alchemical Adding sophistication Class +/-2 elemental ELEMENTAL CLASS MEMBERS: Class 0: Air→Air, Water→Water, Earth→Earth, Fire→Fire Class +1: Air→Water, Water→Earth, Earth→Fire, Fire→Air Class -1: Air→Fire, Water→Air, Earth→Water, Fire→Earth Class +/-2: Air→Earth, Water→Fire, Earth→Air, Fire→Water

• • •

Appendix D: Permanence, Fixation, and Risk

This appendix addresses critical considerations around workings that persist, lock, or become difficult to reverse. Understanding these dynamics enables informed choice rather than accidental entrapment.

D.1 The Permanence Spectrum

Workings exist on a spectrum of permanence: TEMPORARY PERSISTENT SELF-MAINTAINING FIXED (fades naturally) (requires effort (maintains itself) (resists all to maintain) change) | | | | Type I Type II/V Type III Type IV TEMPORARY (Type I): Pattern fades when reinforcement stops Natural decay occurs, flexibility preserved Appropriate for: Exploration, healing, learning, temporary states PERSISTENT (Type II, V): Pattern continues with some momentum Can drift or evolve over time Appropriate for: Building on strength, holding against pressure SELF-MAINTAINING (Type III): Pattern enforces itself without attention Does not fade naturally Appropriate for: Protection, sovereignty, identity shifts FIXED (Type IV): Pattern prevents its own change External force required to break Appropriate for: Seals, vows, absolute boundaries

D.2 What Creates Fixation

Fixation occurs when a pattern becomes self-reinforcing and resists change. TYPE IV CONFIGURATIONS: When H = I = T, everything reinforces everything else. No internal leverage point for change. Structurally sealed. CLASS 0 DYADS: Identity dyads (X→X) create single-force reinforcement with no motion. Multiple Class 0 dyads compound the fixation. TYPE III WITHOUT EXIT VECTORS: When H = T and the achieved state has no natural development path, the destination locks without flexibility. THE CORE TRADEOFF: Fixation trades ADAPTABILITY for STABILITY. Appropriate when: • The threat is severe and ongoing • The commitment should be absolute • The scope is bounded (a space, a relationship, a pattern) NOT appropriate when: • Circumstances may change • Growth and development are needed • The scope is broad (identity, life direction)

D.3 Risk Assessment Model

Risk in this system is ADVISORY, not PROHIBITIVE. The system describes what configurations do; you decide whether those effects serve your purpose. LOW RISK: Type I configurations Class +1 and Class -1 dyads Exit vectors present Natural decay possible MEDIUM RISK: Type II and Type V configurations Sustained single-class patterns Some fixation potential Moderate reversal effort HIGH RISK: Type III configurations (especially without Mirror Inversion) Type IV configurations Class 0 dyads in critical positions No exit vectors, difficult reversal EXTREME RISK: Type IV with Class 0 dyads Black→Black fixation (perpetual dissolution) Systemic configurations affecting identity Multiple compounding fixation factors

D.4 Specific Risk Patterns

BLACK INVOLVEMENT: Low Risk: Black→White, Black→Green, Black→Red (exit present) High Risk: Black→Black (perpetual dissolution, no exit) Mitigation: Always pair extended dissolution with an exit force CLASS 0 COMPOUNDING: Multiple Class 0 dyads create compounded fixation Example: H: Red→Red, I: Red→Red, T: Red→Red → Triple-reinforced sovereignty fixation Mitigation: Limit Class 0 to one position, or use intentionally for sealing TYPE IV + CLASS +/-2: Creates PERMANENT CONTRADICTION The opposition cannot resolve Use only when permanent paradox serves the purpose IDENTITY-LEVEL OPERATIONS: Higher stakes because the pattern shapes who you are Lower risk: Type I or II for identity work Higher risk: Type III/IV for identity installation/sealing

D.5 Mitigation Strategies

INCLUDE EXIT VECTORS: Ensure configuration includes forces with natural development paths Good: Black→White (White can progress to Green) Risk: Black→Black (Black loops to itself) USE MIRROR INVERSION: For Type III, Mirror Inversion creates self-correcting rather than self-locking patterns. Dynamic balance rather than static fixation. BOUND THE SCOPE: Apply high-fixation configurations to bounded scopes: • A specific space rather than all spaces • A specific relationship rather than all relationships • A specific pattern rather than entire identity PREPARE REVERSAL IN ADVANCE: Before deploying high-permanence workings, design your reversal strategy. Know how to undo what you are about to do. USE TEMPORAL BOUNDARIES: Some workings can include temporal limits—they maintain for a set period, then naturally release. TEST BEFORE COMMITTING: For Type IV, consider whether Type III might serve the same purpose with less permanence. Self-maintaining is often sufficient.

• • •

Appendix E: Designing Reversals

The ability to undo work is essential to practitioner sovereignty. Every working should be deployed with understanding of how to reverse it.

E.1 Foundational Principles

AXIOM 1: ALL WORKINGS CAN BE UNDONE Nothing is truly permanent unless you lack knowledge to reverse it. Irreversibility is a choice, not a fate. AXIOM 2: UNDOING IS NOT "UN-HAPPENING" The effects occurred and shaped reality. Reversal means: • Releasing the enforced pattern • Allowing natural motion to resume • Removing artificial constraints Analogy: Undoing is like removing a dam, not reversing the river. AXIOM 3: EASE OF REVERSAL VARIES BY CONFIGURATION Type I: Easiest — pattern is not self-reinforcing Type II: Easy to moderate — return to established origin Type V: Moderate — remove opposition pressure Type III: Difficult — must break host-graft unity Type IV: Most difficult — no internal leverage, requires external force AXIOM 4: TIME AFFECTS REVERSAL COMPLEXITY Recent workings: Easier (pattern not deeply established) Established workings: Harder (reality adapted around them) AXIOM 5: SOME REVERSALS REQUIRE INTERMEDIATE STEPS Complex configurations may need sequential operations to safely unwind.

E.2 The Three Reversal Approaches

DISMANTLE: Active Deconstruction Deploy a new working specifically designed to undo the previous. Properties: Fastest, highest practitioner involvement When to Use: Type III and IV, when speed matters, when complete removal needed Design: Use forces opposing the locked pattern. Black often necessary. TRANSFORM: Redirect Rather Than Undo Deploy a working that supersedes the previous, making original obsolete. Properties: Medium involvement, creates new state rather than return When to Use: When new direction more useful than return, when direct confrontation would cause whiplash Design: New pattern must be strong enough to supersede. DECAY: Allow Natural Dissolution Stop reinforcing the working and let it fade naturally. Properties: Slowest, lowest involvement, gentlest transition When to Use: Type I only, Type II if new origin established elsewhere CRITICAL: Does NOT work for Type III, Type IV, or any self-reinforcing pattern

E.3 Reversal by Configuration Type

REVERSING TYPE I: Strategy: DECAY usually sufficient. Stop maintaining. If active reversal needed: Simple negation or redirect with new Type I REVERSING TYPE II: Strategy: Return to origin (already established) or establish new origin Configuration: Type II with T matching desired return state REVERSING TYPE III: Strategy: Must DISMANTLE or TRANSFORM. Decay will not work. Key: Separate Host from T via new Host, dissolution, or superseding Type III Special Case: Mirror Inversion requires disrupting the feedback mechanism itself REVERSING TYPE IV: Strategy: Apply EXTERNAL FORCE. Internal leverage does not exist. Breaking: Black forces applied from outside; may need sustained effort Multi-Phase: Weaken seal → create crack → establish alternative → supersede REVERSING TYPE V: Strategy: Remove opposition pressure or redirect with supportive host Without pressure to resist, Type V often releases naturally

E.4 Multi-Phase Reversals

WHEN MULTI-PHASE IS NEEDED: • Original working is deeply established • Direct reversal would cause whiplash • Configuration type is III or IV • Multiple mechanical properties need addressing GENERAL MULTI-PHASE STRUCTURE: Phase 1: WEAKEN Apply initial dissolution or loosening Create space for change Duration: Days to weeks Phase 2: REDIRECT Establish alternative pattern Begin shifting energy to new configuration Duration: Weeks to months Phase 3: COMPLETE Finalize new pattern Release remnants of old Confirm reversal is stable

E.5 Reversal Quick Reference

BY CONFIGURATION TYPE: CONFIG TYPE DIFFICULTY PRIMARY APPROACH KEY PRINCIPLE ─────────── ────────── ──────────────── ───────────── Type I Easy Decay or Dismantle Stop maintaining Type II Moderate Return or Transform Return to origin Type III Difficult Dismantle or Break host-graft Transform unity Type IV Very Difficult Dismantle with External force, external force no internal leverage Type V Moderate Remove pressure Opposition sustains it BY APPROACH: APPROACH SPEED EFFORT WORKS FOR ──────── ───── ────── ───────── Decay Slow Low Type I, some II/V Transform Medium Medium Any, when new direction preferred Dismantle Fast High Type III, IV, or when speed needed

• • •

Appendix F: From Use Case to Configuration

This appendix provides a complete workflow for designing your own workings, from initial intent through final configuration. Follow these steps to move beyond recipes to independent working design.

F.1 The Design Workflow Overview

STEP 1: Articulate Your Use Case ↓ STEP 2: Analyze the Language ↓ STEP 3: Identify Forces Needed ↓ STEP 4: Determine Configuration Type ↓ STEP 5: Select Dyad Classes ↓ STEP 6: Construct the Dyads ↓ STEP 7: Select Elemental Mode ↓ STEP 8: Verify and Adjust ↓ STEP 9: Design the Reversal ↓ STEP 10: Write the Charge

F.2 Steps 1-3: Use Case to Forces

STEP 1: ARTICULATE YOUR USE CASE Write out what you want to accomplish in plain language. Be specific. Good: "I want to establish protection around my home that maintains itself without my constant attention." Poor: "I want protection." (Too vague) STEP 2: ANALYZE THE LANGUAGE Identify verbs, intensity markers, and relationship markers. Verbs: action words → map to forces Intensity: "gradual" vs "breakthrough" vs "absolute" Relationship: "X into Y", "X within Y", "X despite Y" STEP 3: IDENTIFY FORCES NEEDED Map verbs to alchemical and elemental forces. BLACK: dissolve, release, clear, break down, let go, face fear, sever WHITE: purify, clarify, refine, simplify, filter, essence, precision GREEN: grow, expand, open, generate, create, develop, connect, abundant RED: manifest, embody, claim, establish, sovereign, complete, protect AIR: thought, communication, strategy, mental processes WATER: emotion, intuition, feeling, receptivity, flow EARTH: building, grounding, materializing, stability FIRE: action, will, transformation, urgency, catalysis

F.3 Steps 4-6: Type, Class, and Dyads

STEP 4: DETERMINE CONFIGURATION TYPE Should fade naturally → Type I Should persist but adapt → Type II or V Should maintain itself → Type III Must be absolutely permanent → Type IV Building on existing strength? → Type II (H = I) Holding against opposition? → Type V (H ≠ I = T) STEP 5: SELECT DYAD CLASSES Breakthrough/Opening: Class +/-2 (dialectical tension) Developmental/Growth: Class +1 (progressive flow) Maintenance/Stability: Class 0 (fixation) Return/Integration: Class -1 (regressive grounding) STEP 6: CONSTRUCT THE DYADS HOST (H): What context should transformation occur within? For Type II: H = starting state For Type III: H = ending state For Type IV: H = both INITIAL GRAFT (I): Where are you starting? What force describes current state or raw material? TERMINAL GRAFT (T): Where are you ending? What force describes desired outcome?

F.4 Steps 7-10: Elemental, Verify, Reversal, Charge

STEP 7: SELECT ELEMENTAL MODE Outer (operational category): Mental/Strategic → Air outer Emotional → Water outer Physical → Earth outer Action/Crisis → Fire outer Inner (operational goal): Same as outer (Class 0): Pure modal reinforcement +1 from outer: Natural development -1 from outer: Grounding or corrective +/-2 from outer: Complex integration STEP 8: VERIFY AND ADJUST [ ] Configuration type matches permanence needs [ ] Classes match intensity [ ] Forces present match use case verbs [ ] Transition (I → T) describes desired change [ ] Risk level is understood and accepted STEP 9: DESIGN THE REVERSAL Original Type I → Decay or simple Type I reversal Original Type II → Type II returning to origin Original Type III → Type II or III with dissolution Original Type IV → Type II with strong dissolution, multi-phase STEP 10: WRITE THE CHARGE 1. State the current situation (optional) 2. Declare what forces are acting 3. Describe the transformation 4. Affirm the end state 5. Seal the working Be specific, declarative, present tense, complete.

F.5 Troubleshooting Common Issues

CONFIGURATION FEELS TOO WEAK: • Shift from Type I to Type III • Change Class +1 to Class +/-2 • Check resonance between elemental and alchemical CONFIGURATION FEELS TOO EXTREME: • Shift from Type IV to Type III • Use progressive rather than dialectical classes • Remove unnecessary Class 0 dyads CAN'T IDENTIFY THE RIGHT FORCES: • Return to use case and list more verbs • Ask "what needs to happen?" more specifically • Consider what force would CREATE the desired state UNSURE ABOUT CONFIGURATION TYPE: • Focus on permanence question first • Ask "should this maintain itself?" • Ask "am I building on something or creating new?" REVERSAL DESIGN IS UNCLEAR: • Identify what makes the working persist • Match reversal approach to configuration type • When in doubt, design for Dismantle approach

Appendix G: Creating the Machinery

This appendix explains how the Alchemental Enochiana system was discovered and why it works. Understanding the architecture behind the machinery deepens practice and reveals why repetition strengthens workings safely.

G.1 The Mirror Principle: How This System Was Discovered

The entire system emerged from a single observation: when Spirit is placed in the center column of the Tablet of Union (AONT rather than the traditional EHNB), the elemental attributions of the Tablet of Union match those of the Servient Section exactly.

This was the first mirror.

Tablet of Union (Spirit Centered) Servient Section ──────────────────────────────── ──────────────── Row 1: Air Row 3: Air Row 2: Water Row 4: Water Row 3: Earth Row 5: Earth Row 4: Fire Row 6: Fire Column 1: Air Column 1: Air Column 2: Water Column 2: Water Column 3: Spirit Column 3: Spirit Column 4: Earth Column 4: Earth Column 5: Fire Column 5: Fire

This correspondence revealed that the Tablet of Union is an incomplete Subangle. The Kerubic row (Row 1) and Commanding row (Row 2) are not present on the Tablet of Union. These rows are supplied by the Operator.

From this first mirror, others emerged:

STRUCTURAL MIRRORS WITHIN THE SUBANGLE The Kerubic Angel (Row 1, horizontal) mirrors the Commanding Angel (Row 2) The Servient Angel (Rows 3-6, horizontal) mirrors the Commanding Angel The Ruling Angel (vertical column) mirrors the Summoning Angel (Column 3) These mirrors reveal: Compelling will gives way to intent and action. Authority gives way to form. Intent given form results in action. NAME LENGTH MIRRORS Kerubic Circuit: 5, 5, 4, 3, 3 (Archangelic, Mercurial, Base, Regent, Rooted) Servient Circuit: 5, 5, 4, 3, 3 (same structure) God Names: 3, 4, 5 The God Names (3, 4, 5) are the inverted mirror of the circuit names (5, 5, 4, 3, 3), with 4 as the center point. THE THREE CROSSES Black Cross: The Tablet of Union cross (Spirit domain) Great Cross: The Watchtower cross (God Names domain) Calvary Cross: The Subangle cross (Operational domain) Each polarity of power flows through a cross before converging in the Subangle. The fractal nature of the Great Table comes from this mirroring at every level. THE SPIRAL MIRRORS King: Clockwise spiral around the Great Cross Mighty Prince: Tighter clockwise spiral around the Great Cross Prince: Clockwise spiral around the Calvary Cross The Prince's spiral around the Calvary Cross mirrors the King and Mighty Prince spirals around the Great Cross. The same pattern at different scales—another fractal echo.

Every mirror discovered has revealed more hidden knowledge about the system. The mirrors are not decorative—they are structural. The Great Table is fractal because of this mirroring. Each level contains the pattern of the other levels. This is why a grafted Subangle can function as a complete working unit: it contains the whole pattern in miniature.

G.2 The Operator as Source

The Tablet of Union is an incomplete Subangle. The Operator completes it.

When you perform a working, you provide:

Row 1 (Kerubic Row): Divine Intent Row 2 (Commanding Row): Divine Compelling Will

These two rows are not received from external sources. You supply them. This is the foundational stance of the system: the Operator stands above the machinery, never beneath it.

Your Kerubic and Commanding rows provide the root for:

Center Column: Archangel of Archangels (Divine Authority) Elemental Columns: Ruling Angel (Divine Form)

Both connect to the Servient Archangel (Divine Action).

Through intent and compelling will, you direct divine action by defining form while operating from a position of authority. This is not petition. This is operation. You are not asking permission. You are configuring an engine.

All humans have the spark of the Divine within them. This is what gives you the authority to interface with the Tablet of Union. You are Divinity incarnate, and your intent and will are the power source for the entire system.

G.3 The Dual Polarity Architecture

Power flows into the Subangle through two polarities. Understanding this architecture explains why the machinery works and why the Servient Angel is the point of contact with physical reality.

Polarity 1: Humanity's Projection onto Source (God Name Descent)

The three God Names of each Watchtower are humanity's tripartite projection onto Source. Humans always create God in their image to understand some aspect of the Divine. The God Names are this veil of understanding.

Power flows from Source through this veil:

Source (Operator) | v Three God Names (humanity's understanding of the Divine) | v King (solar director and conductor) | v Six Seniors (planetary densities attenuating God energy into forms reality can understand) | v Mighty Prince (receptive solar aspect, tighter spiral, gathers power) | v Prince of the Subangle (distributes to the Calvary Cross) | v Calvary Cross Arms: Commanding Angel (Divine Compelling Will) Calvary Cross Spine: Summoning Angel (Divine Authority)

The King and Mighty Prince spiral clockwise around the Great Cross. The Mighty Prince's spiral is tighter, carrying an attenuated frequency. The Prince of the Subangle spirals around the Calvary Cross, mimicking this structure at a smaller scale.

From the Calvary Cross, energy distributes to the angel names:

Above the arms: Kerubic Angel (Divine Intent) Below the arms: Servient Angel (Divine Action) Connecting them: Ruling Angel (Divine Form)
Polarity 2: Source's Direct Emanation (Tablet of Union Descent)

The three Holy Names of the Tablet of Union are Source's projection outward—Source's tripartite manifestation. Where the God Names are humanity's projection onto Source (humanity creating God in its image), the Tablet of Union names are Source's projection into creation.

Power flows directly from the Tablet of Union through the Archangels:

Tablet of Union | v Archangel of Archangels (center column: AONT/ONTA/NTAO/TAON) Ruling Archangel (elemental column: EHNB/XCAI/RMTO/PAAM etc.) Servient Archangel (elemental row: EXARP/HCOMA/NANTA/BITOM etc.)

These three Archangels provide the prefixes for the Subangular names:

Archangel of Archangels --> prefix for Archangelic Kerubic Angel Ruling Archangel --> prefix for Archangelic Ruling Angel Servient Archangel --> prefix for Archangelic Servient Angel (and for all four Cacodaemons)

The Archangelic names are the "wires" carrying Tablet of Union energy:

Archangelic Kerubic Angel (prefix + base Kerubic) Archangelic Ruling Angel (prefix + base Ruling) Archangelic Servient Angel (prefix + base Servient) | v Kerubic Regent Cacodaemon (consequence of intent enacted) Kerubic Rooted Cacodaemon (reaction to consequence) Servient Regent Cacodaemon (consequence of action taken) Servient Rooted Cacodaemon (reaction to consequence)
The Mercurial Connection

The Mercurial versions of the Kerubic, Ruling, and Servient Angels are mid-fixed with a letter from the Calvary Cross:

Mercurial Kerubic: Base Kerubic + letter from Row 1, Column 3 Mercurial Ruling: Base Ruling + letter from Row 2 in same column Mercurial Servient: Base Servient + letter from Column 3 in same row

The Mercurial names are the "wires" carrying Calvary Cross energy—the attenuated God energy that descended through the King, Seniors, and Princes.

The Base Names as Connection Point

The base names (Kerubic, Ruling, Servient) share their four letters with both the Archangelic versions and the Mercurial versions:

Archangelic Kerubic = prefix + [base Kerubic letters] Mercurial Kerubic = [base Kerubic letters] + mid-fix Base Kerubic = the shared four letters

This overlap makes the base names the connection point where both polarities converge. The Archangelic names carry Tablet of Union energy. The Mercurial names carry Calvary Cross energy. The base names receive both.

The Convergence Points

The Ruling Angel bridges the Kerubic and Servient. But both the Kerubic and Servient Angels—along with their Cacodaemons—are points of contact with reality. They work together as a scalpel to carve a path through existence:

Kerubic Angel: Connection to the Ethereal world ("Above") Intent manifesting in the realm of mind and spirit Servient Angel: Connection to the Corporeal world ("Below") Action manifesting in the realm of matter and form

As above, so below. The working cuts through both realms simultaneously. The Kerubic circuit shapes the ethereal conditions; the Servient circuit shapes the corporeal conditions. Together, they produce complete manifestation.

The Complete Circuit
POLARITY 1 POLARITY 2 (God Names) (Tablet of Union) | | v v King --> Seniors --> Mighty Prince Archangel of Archangels | Ruling Archangel v Servient Archangel Prince of Subangle | | v v Archangelic Subangular Angels Calvary Cross and Cacodaemons (Commanding, Summoning) (Tablet of Union/Black Cross wires) | | v | Mercurial Angels | (Calvary Cross wires) | | | +-------------------+-------------------+ | v Base Angels (Kerubic, Ruling, Servient) [connection point] | v Kerubic Angel + Cacodaemons (Ethereal contact / "Above") | Servient Angel + Cacodaemons (Corporeal contact / "Below")

G.4 The Cacodaemons

The Cacodaemons are not byproducts or optional components. They are active parts of the circuit and essential to the prayer.

There are four Cacodaemons in each working:

Kerubic Regent Cacodaemon: Consequence of intent enacted Kerubic Rooted Cacodaemon: Equal and opposite reaction to consequence Servient Regent Cacodaemon: Consequence of action taken Servient Rooted Cacodaemon: Equal and opposite reaction to consequence
Regent vs. Rooted

The difference between Regent and Rooted Cacodaemons is structural:

Regent Cacodaemons share a letter with the Ruling Angel. They are bound by Divine Form. Rooted Cacodaemons share no letters with the Ruling Angel—only their base angel and the prefix. They are unbound by Divine Form.

The Regent Cacodaemons represent consequences that operate within the structure of the working. The Rooted Cacodaemons represent the reaction that operates outside that structure—the equal and opposite force that balances the working in the larger system.

The Kerubic and Servient Circuits

The prayer calls the names in two circuits:

Kerubic Circuit: Archangelic Kerubic (5 letters) Mercurial Kerubic (5 letters) Kerubic Base (4 letters) Kerubic Regent Cacodaemon (3 letters) Kerubic Rooted Cacodaemon (3 letters) Servient Circuit: Archangelic Servient (5 letters) Mercurial Servient (5 letters) Servient Base (4 letters) Servient Regent Cacodaemon (3 letters) Servient Rooted Cacodaemon (3 letters)

Both circuits follow the pattern 5, 5, 4, 3, 3. The God Names follow the pattern 3, 4, 5. This is an inverted mirror with 4 as the center point.

G.5 The Encoding Principle

When you graft a Subangle, you are encoding intention into structure.

The Host dyad determines the stable environment and governing context. The Initial Graft determines the starting state being transformed. The Terminal Graft determines the achieved state being manifested. The Elemental dyad determines how the transformation propagates.

These four components, when grafted together, produce a specific alchemical transmutation. The encoding is not something you add—it is what the grafted structure IS.

This is why the system produces specific, predictable effects. The selection of dyads defines the meaning. The grafting process constructs the machinery. The names derived from that machinery carry the encoded intention.

G.6 Repetition and Strengthening

Because intention is encoded in the structure itself, repetition strengthens workings safely.

When you recite the prayer and names, you establish the circuitry in the causal field around you. You are calling on a piece of the Fractal—the Great Table—and activating it for your use.

If the working is active: Repetition adds charge and strengthens the signal. If the working has faded: Repetition reactivates the circuit.

The goal of repetition is to "lock in" the frequency of the transmutation. Each recitation reinforces the same stable pattern because the machinery itself encodes the intention. There is no drift, no variation, no muddying of purpose.

This is fundamentally different from approaches that depend on emotional state or visualization consistency. The machinery holds the pattern. You simply power it.

G.7 Contrast with Emotional Transmutation

Emotional Transmutation is a valid magical technique. It uses the practitioner's emotional state as the vehicle for magical intention. Strong emotion, properly directed, can charge a working powerfully.

The problem with repeated Emotional Transmutation is that emotional states are fickle. Your emotional experience of "protection" today may differ from your experience next week. Repeated emotional transmutation across sessions introduces variation—it "muddies the waters" because each repetition carries slightly different emotional content.

The machinery approach avoids this problem. The intention is encoded in the structure, not in your emotional state. Repetition reinforces the same pattern regardless of how you feel on a given day.

G.8 Combining Approaches

The machinery approach and Emotional Transmutation are not mutually exclusive. Used together correctly, they can provide significant power boost while maintaining long-term stability.

The key is timing:

Initial Working (Same Session)

When you first perform a working, your intention is fresh and clear. This is the ideal moment for Emotional Transmutation. You can:

1. Recite the prayer 2. Deliver the charge 3. Perform Emotional Transmutation to reinforce the charge

If you are also creating a sigil (see Sigil Creation below), you can perform Emotional Transmutation again when charging the completed sigil. Both transmutations occur in the same session while intention is fresh—this is safe and powerful.

The combination bridges two co-transmutative acts: the structural encoding of the machinery and the emotional power of directed feeling. Together, they give the initial operation significant boost.

Subsequent Repetitions (Later Sessions)

After the initial working, use the machinery alone. Recite the prayer. Deliver the charge. Do not attempt Emotional Transmutation.

The machinery maintains the pattern. Your emotional state on repetition day does not affect the encoded intention. This provides long-term stability and safe strengthening.

G.9 Sigil Creation from the Grafted Subangle

A sigil condenses the machinery into visual form. It encodes the entire grafted Subangle in a single drawn shape that can be used alongside the prayer or in other workings.

The Source Letters

The sigil is created from the 24 letters used in name derivation:

• 3 prefix letters: The vertical prefix beside the Kerubic row (Row 1) The vertical prefix beside the Servient row (the row of your Elemental) The horizontal prefix above the Ruling Angel column (first letter column) • Row 1: The Kerubic section (4 letters, excluding Column 3) • Row 2: The Calvary Cross arms (5 letters) • Column 3: The Calvary Cross spine (letters from Rows 1, 3, 4, 5, 6) • The Servient row: The row matching your Elemental dyad's Macro element (4 letters, excluding Column 3) • The first letter column: The column matching your Elemental dyad's Micro element (letters from Rows 3, 4, 5, 6 excluding the Servient row letter already counted)

The exact letters depend on your Elemental dyad, which determines which Servient Angel you use and therefore which row and column contribute letters.

Example: Sigil Source for Earth to Water

Using the configuration Host White to Red, Elemental Earth to Water, Initial Black to White, Terminal Green to Red:

The Elemental dyad Earth to Water places the Servient Angel at Row 5, Column 2.

Macro Earth = Row 5 (Servient row) Micro Water = Column 2 (first letter column)

The fully grafted Subangle with prefixes:

The Creation Process
1. Write out the 24 source letters 2. Begin combining letter shapes freeform. Unlike a linear sequence of letters, the Subangle has both length and width. Letters can combine vertically as well as horizontally. This 2D structure may inspire approaches different from traditional letter-combination methods. 3. Iterate. Combine the resulting shapes further. Simplify toward a single drawn shape. 4. Continue until the shape looks right to you. This is aesthetic intuition—there is no external criterion. The sigil is yours. 5. The final shape is your sigil. It encodes the entire grafted Subangle machinery.
Charging the Sigil

If you create the sigil in the same session as your first prayer recitation, you can charge it with Emotional Transmutation while intention is fresh.

Draw the final sigil. Hold your intention. Direct emotional energy into the shape. The sigil receives both the structural encoding (from the letters) and the emotional charge (from your directed feeling).

After this initial charging, the sigil can be used without Emotional Transmutation—the structural encoding persists.

Sigil Use

The sigil functions as both summary and parallel:

Summary: Use alongside the prayer as a visual condensation of the machinery. The sigil represents the working in compact form. Parallel: Use independently in other workings to represent the transmutation. The sigil carries the encoded intention and can be incorporated into other magical operations.

The sigil provides a potent, stable charge because it encodes the machinery structurally rather than depending on repeated emotional consistency.
